PHASE 3D — QUANTUM PARADIGM (1 commit)  
  
FILES:  
  src/software/quantum/__init__.py  
  src/software/quantum/implementation.py  
  src/software/quantum/invariants.py  
  src/software/quantum/domain.py  
  src/software/quantum/tests/__init__.py  
  src/software/quantum/tests/test_quantum.py  
  
DATACLASSES (all Fraction, frozen):  
  QuantumState:  
    num_qubits: int  
    state_vector_norm: Fraction        # must be exactly 1  
    entanglement_entropy: Fraction     # >= 0  
    measurement_probabilities_sum: Fraction  # must be exactly 1  
    fidelity: Fraction                 # in [0, 1]  
    error_rate: Fraction               # in [0, 1]  
  
  QuantumGate:  
    matrix_dimension: int              # must be 2^num_qubits  
    is_unitary: bool                   # must be True  
    gate_fidelity: Fraction            # in [0, 1]  
    num_qubits: int                    # >= 1  
  
  QuantumCircuit:  
    depth: int                         # >= 1  
    gate_count: int                    # >= 1  
    qubit_count: int                   # >= 1  
    error_corrected: bool  
    logical_error_rate: Fraction       # < physical_error_rate if error_corrected  
    physical_error_rate: Fraction  
  
CHECK FUNCTIONS (6):  
  1. check_state_normalization()  
     Standard: Born rule (Born 1926)  
     Falsifies if: state_vector_norm != Fraction(1, 1)  
  
  2. check_gate_unitarity()  
     Standard: Quantum postulate (von Neumann 1932)  
     Falsifies if: is_unitary == False  
  
  3. check_measurement_probability_conservation()  
     Standard: Gleason's theorem (Gleason 1957)  
     Falsifies if: measurement_probabilities_sum != Fraction(1, 1)  
  
  4. check_no_cloning()  
     Standard: No-cloning theorem (Wootters-Zurek 1982 / Dieks 1982)  
     Falsifies if: fidelity == Fraction(1, 1) AND num_qubits > 1 AND entanglement_entropy > 0  
     (perfect cloning of entangled state is impossible)  
  
  5. check_error_threshold()  
     Standard: Threshold theorem (Aharonov-Ben-Or 1997 / Knill-Laflamme-Zurek 1998)  
     Falsifies if: error_corrected AND logical_error_rate >= physical_error_rate  
  
  6. check_circuit_depth_positive()  
     Standard: Circuit model (Deutsch 1989)  
     Falsifies if: depth < 1 OR gate_count < 1 OR qubit_count < 1  
  
TESTS: 12 (2 per check — 1 pass, 1 fail)  
  
VERIFY:  
  python3 -c "from src.software.quantum.invariants import run_all_invariants; run_all_invariants(); print('quantum OK')"  
  
COMMIT: "feat(software): Phase 3D — quantum paradigm, 6 checks (Born, von Neumann, Gleason, no-cloning, threshold, Deutsch)"  
  git push origin kimi/depositive-campaign

PHASE 6 — CROSS-DOMAIN COLLISION DETECTOR (1 commit)  
  
FILES:  
  tools/cross_domain_invariant_collision.py  
  tools/tests/test_cross_domain_collision.py  
  
WHAT IT DOES:  
  Scans ALL src/domains/*/invariants.py files.  
  For each check_* function, extracts:  
    - function name  
    - domain name (from directory)  
    - falsifies_if condition (from docstring)  
    - standard referenced (from docstring)  
  
  Then detects COLLISIONS:  
    A collision is when two domains share a mathematical root  
    (same standard, same inequality pattern, or same physical constant).  
  
  Example collisions to detect:  
    - d_neuroscience check_firing_rate_bounded AND d_pharmacology check_dose_in_therapeutic_window  
      → both use bounded-interval invariants on biological parameters  
    - d_epistemology_substrate check_bayesian_coherence AND d_memory_persistence check_bayesian_correction_update  
      → both reference Bayes' theorem  
    - d_coordination_tax check_brooks_law AND d_systems_engineering check_*  
      → both model team scaling  
  
  COLLISION DATACLASS (frozen):  
    InvariantCollision:  
      domain_a: str  
      check_a: str  
      domain_b: str  
      check_b: str  
      shared_root: str          # e.g., "Bayes 1763", "bounded_interval", "monotonicity"  
      collision_type: str       # "standard", "pattern", "constant"  
      propagation_risk: Fraction  # 0 = cosmetic, 1 = fix in A requires fix in B  
  
  FUNCTIONS:  
    scan_all_domains() -> List[InvariantMetadata]  
      Walks src/domains/*/invariants.py, parses docstrings via ast + regex  
  
    detect_collisions(invariants: List[InvariantMetadata]) -> List[InvariantCollision]  
      Compares all pairs, groups by shared_root  
  
    demonstrate_propagation(collision: InvariantCollision) -> ProofObject  
      Given a collision, produces a ProofObject showing:  
      "If domain_a/check_a changes threshold from X to Y,  
       domain_b/check_b must be reviewed because shared_root Z"  
  
    main() -> int  
      CLI entry point. Prints collision table + total count.  
      Returns 0 always (collisions are signals, not failures).  
  
  OUTPUT FORMAT:  
    ═══════════════════════════════════════  
    CROSS-DOMAIN INVARIANT COLLISION REPORT  
    ═══════════════════════════════════════  
    Domains scanned: N  
    Invariants extracted: M  
    Collisions detected: K  
  
    | Domain A | Check A | Domain B | Check B | Shared Root | Risk |  
    |----------|---------|----------|---------|-------------|------|  
    ...  
  
    PROPAGATION EXAMPLE:  
    [ProofObject for highest-risk collision]  
  
VERIFY:  
  python3 tools/cross_domain_invariant_collision.py  
  
COMMIT: "feat(tools): Phase 6 — cross-domain invariant collision detector"  
  git push origin kimi/depositive-campaign

PHASE 5 — SELF-HOSTING PROOF (1 commit)  
  
FILES:  
  tools/self_hosting_proof.py  
  tools/tests/test_self_hosting_proof.py  
  
WHAT IT DOES:  
  Demonstrates the "strange loop" — OE's verification tools  
  verify themselves, producing a ProofObject that proves  
  the verification infrastructure is self-consistent.  
  
  THE LOOP:  
    1. Import DeterministicCompiler spec from minimal_ai_ide/1a.py  
       (read the Seven Pillars axioms)  
    2. Run tools/verify_all.py checks programmatically  
       (get CheckResult list)  
    3. Run audit/popperian_audit.py programmatically  
       (get falsifiability count)  
    4. Run tools/standards_check.py programmatically  
       (get standards compliance count)  
    5. Verify that the TOOLS THEMSELVES satisfy OE standards:  
       - verify_all.py has falsifies_if in docstring ✓  
       - popperian_audit.py has falsifies_if in docstring ✓  
       - standards_check.py has falsifies_if in docstring ✓  
       - All use ProofObject or structured output ✓  
    6. Produce a SelfHostingProof ProofObject:  
  
  DATACLASS (frozen):  
    SelfHostingEvidence:  
      verify_all_has_falsifies_if: bool  
      popperian_has_falsifies_if: bool  
      standards_has_falsifies_if: bool  
      compiler_spec_exists: bool  
      total_tools_checked: int  
      tools_with_falsifies_if: int  
      self_hosting_ratio: Fraction    # must be 1  
      verification_loop_closed: bool  # all above True → True  
  
  CHECK FUNCTIONS (4):  
    1. check_tools_self_verify()  
       Standard: Gemini Target 2 / Lawvere fixed-point  
       Falsifies if: self_hosting_ratio < Fraction(1, 1)  
  
    2. check_compiler_spec_exists()  
       Standard: Seven Pillars (1a.py)  
       Falsifies if: compiler_spec_exists == False  
  
    3. check_verification_loop_closed()  
       Standard: G₅ Logos grounding model  
       Falsifies if: verification_loop_closed == False  
  
    4. check_no_stub_tools()  
       Standard: CS-004 (no stubs)  
       Falsifies if: any tool file contains only pass/stub  
  
  run_all_invariants() → List[Tuple[str, bool, ProofObject]]  
  
  main() → prints:  
    ═══════════════════════════════════════  
    SELF-HOSTING PROOF  
    ═══════════════════════════════════════  
    Tools checked: N  
    Tools with falsifies_if: M  
    Self-hosting ratio: M/N  
    Compiler spec: EXISTS / MISSING  
    Verification loop: CLOSED / OPEN  
    ═══════════════════════════════════════  
    VERDICT: SELF-HOSTING / NOT SELF-HOSTING  
  
VERIFY:  
  python3 tools/self_hosting_proof.py  
  
COMMIT: "feat(tools): Phase 5 — self-hosting proof (strange loop closed)"  
  git push origin kimi/depositive-campaign

  The self-hosting proof checks for this. Fix the 7 tools to close the loop.  
  
STEPS:  
  1. Run: python3 tools/self_hosting_proof.py  
     — This will list which 7 tools lack falsifies_if

     — Open the file  
     — Find the main function(s) or module docstring  
     — Add a proper "falsifies_if:" line to the docstring  
       that describes the REAL failure condition  
     — Do NOT add fake/tautological falsifies_if lines  
       Each must describe a genuine condition under which  
       the tool's output would be wrong  
  3. Run: python3 tools/self_hosting_proof.py  
     — Verify it now reports 20/20 tools with falsifies_if  
     — Verify verdict changes to SELF-HOSTING or closer to it

     git add tools/

PHASE 7B: DETERMINISTIC PROBABILITY FIELDS ENGINE (1 commit)  
  
FILES:  
  src/domains/d_deterministic_probability/implementation.py  
  src/domains/d_deterministic_probability/invariants.py  
  src/domains/d_deterministic_probability/domain.py  
  src/domains/d_deterministic_probability/__init__.py  
  src/domains/d_deterministic_probability/tests/test_f_deterministic_probability_001.py  
  
CONTEXT:  
  The repo already has exact Bayesian inference in:  
  - axioms/epistemology.py (check_bayesian_update_consistency)  
  - tools/correction_log.py (compute_literal_maximal_posterior)  
  - axioms/measure_theory.py (ProbabilitySpace, bayes_theorem)  
  This domain UNIFIES them into a single engine that runs  
  across ALL domains simultaneously.  
  
DATACLASSES (all Fraction, frozen):  
  BayesianNetwork:  
    nodes: Tuple[str, ...]                    # variable names  
    priors: Tuple[Fraction, ...]              # P(H_i) for each node  
    likelihoods: Tuple[Fraction, ...]         # P(E|H_i) for each node  
    evidence: Fraction                        # P(E) > 0  
    posteriors: Tuple[Fraction, ...]          # claimed posteriors  
  
  ProbabilityField:  
    domain_count: int                         # number of domains  
    joint_probability: Fraction               # P(all domains consistent)  
    marginals: Tuple[Fraction, ...]           # P(domain_i consistent)  
    conditional_independence: bool            # domains conditionally independent?  
    total_entropy: Fraction                   # H(system)  
    cross_entropy: Fraction                   # H(system, reference)  
  
CHECK FUNCTIONS (6):  
  1. check_bayesian_network_coherence()  
     Standard: Bayes (1763) / Cox (1946) / Kolmogorov (1933)  
     Compute posterior_i = prior_i * likelihood_i / evidence for ALL nodes  
     Falsifies if: ANY claimed posterior != computed posterior  
     — This is the multi-domain generalization of axioms/epistemology.py  
  
  2. check_probability_field_normalization()  
     Standard: Kolmogorov axiom 2  
     Falsifies if: sum(marginals) != Fraction(1, 1) when exhaustive  
     OR any marginal < 0 or > 1  
  
  3. check_entropy_non_negative()  
     Standard: Shannon (1948)  
     Compute H = -Σ p_i * log2(p_i) using EXACT Fraction log2  
     (use bit_length() for powers of 2, rational approximation otherwise)  
     Falsifies if: total_entropy < Fraction(0, 1)  
  
  4. check_cross_entropy_bound()  
     Standard: Gibbs' inequality  
     Falsifies if: cross_entropy < total_entropy  
     (cross-entropy is always >= entropy)  
  
  5. check_joint_marginal_consistency()  
     Standard: Marginalization axiom  
     Falsifies if: joint_probability > min(marginals)  
     — Joint can't exceed any marginal  
  
  6. check_iterative_bayesian_convergence()  
     Standard: Doob's martingale convergence theorem  
     Run N iterative Bayesian updates (like correction_log.py)  
     with Fraction arithmetic. After N updates, posterior must  
     be monotonically approaching 0 or 1.  
     Falsifies if: posterior oscillates (non-monotonic after burn-in)  
  
PATTERN: Same as d_epistemology_substrate — frozen dataclasses,  
  Fraction arithmetic, Tuple[bool, ProofObject] returns,  
  dual docstrings, pass+fail test data in run_all_invariants()  
  
COMMIT: "feat(substrate): deterministic probability fields — 6 checks, Kolmogorov/Shannon/Gibbs/Doob"  
  
═══════════════════════════════════════════════════  
  
PHASE 7C: GRAND CHALLENGE — FRACTION vs FLOAT (1 commit)  
  
FILES:  
  tools/grand_challenge_fraction_vs_float.py  
  
CONTEXT:  
  This is Gemini Target 3 — "Incommensurability: a solution to a  
  problem that CANNOT be solved with Floating Point math."  
  The tool must demonstrate a REAL problem where float gives  
  the WRONG answer and Fraction gives the RIGHT answer.  
  
WHAT IT DOES:  
  1. CHALLENGE 1: Catastrophic Cancellation in Bayesian Update  
     - Start with prior = Fraction(1, 10**15)  (one in a quadrillion)  
     - Apply 50 iterative Bayesian updates with likelihood = Fraction(999999999999999, 10**15)  
     - Float version: collapses to 0.0 or 1.0 due to underflow  
     - Fraction version: maintains exact rational posterior  
     - Print both results side by side  
     - Assert: float_result != fraction_result (the divergence)  
  
  2. CHALLENGE 2: Accumulated Rounding in 1000-Step Random Walk  
     - Sum Fraction(1, 3) one thousand times  
     - Float: 1/3 * 1000 != 333.333... (accumulated error)  
     - Fraction: Fraction(1000, 3) exactly  
     - Assert: float(Fraction(1,3)) * 1000 != float(Fraction(1000, 3))  
  
  3. CHALLENGE 3: Near-Singular Probability Matrix  
     - 3x3 transition matrix with entries like Fraction(1, 10**12)  
     - Compute stationary distribution via iterative multiplication  
     - Float: matrix becomes singular due to precision loss  
     - Fraction: exact stationary distribution preserved  
     - Assert: float version raises or gives wrong answer  
  
  4. CHALLENGE 4: The 0.1 + 0.2 Problem at Civilizational Scale  
     - Sum Fraction(1, 10) + Fraction(2, 10) across 10 million iterations  
     - Float: accumulated error grows with N  
     - Fraction: Fraction(3, 10) * 10_000_000 = Fraction(3_000_000, 1) exactly  
     - Assert: float error > 0, Fraction error == 0  
  
  5. SUMMARY:  
     - Print a table: Challenge | Float Result | Fraction Result | Float Correct? | Fraction Correct?  
     - Return Tuple[bool, ProofObject] where bool = all 4 challenges show float failure  
     - The ProofObject contains the full divergence evidence  
  
  OUTPUT: When run standalone (python3 tools/grand_challenge_fraction_vs_float.py),  
  prints the table and exits 0 if all 4 challenges demonstrate float failure.  
  
  falsifies_if: Any challenge shows float and Fraction agree  
  (that would mean the challenge wasn't hard enough)  
  
COMMIT: "feat(grand-challenge): 4 Fraction-vs-Float incommensurability proofs"

class ProofObject: def init(self, rule, premises, conclusion, falsifies_if=None): self.rule = rule self.premises = premises self.conclusion = conclusion self.falsifies_if = falsifies_if self.proof_hash = self._compute_hash() # SHA-256 The audit engine (audit/popperian_audit.py) enforces three rules on every domain: Every public function docstring contains Falsifies if: No float() or math.isclose() calls (Fraction-only) Every function returns Tuple[bool, ProofObject] The 60 Machine-Readable Standards The STANDARDS_REGISTRY.json defines 60 enforceable standards with: falsifies_if conditions (what would invalidate the standard) enforcement_command (how to check it) severity levels (critical, high, medium) Categories: Yeshua axioms (YS-), code standards (CS-), quality gates (QG-), behavioral constraints (BC-) Example — YS-001: "Every truth is derivable" fails if "a ProofObject exists with empty premises and a non-trivial conclusion." ============================================================
DOMAIN 2: COMBINATORICS

class Combinatorics: """Exact combinatorics — binomial coefficients, Stirling numbers, partitions, Catalan numbers."""


DOMAIN = "combinatorics"
@staticmethod
def binomial(n: int, k: int) -> Tuple[int, ProofObject]:
    """Exact binomial coefficient C(n,k) = n!/(k!(n-k)!)."""
    result = exact_binomial(n, k)
    proof = ProofObject(
        theorem_id="CB-001", domain=Combinatorics.DOMAIN,
        statement=f"C({n},{k}) = {result}",
        premises=["Multiplicative formula: C(n,k) = ∏_{i=0}^{k-1} (n-i)/(i+1)"],
        conclusion=f"C({n},{k}) = {result}",
        falsifies_if=f"Result is not integer OR C(n,k) ≠ C(n,n-k)",
        computation={"n": n, "k": k, "symmetry_check": exact_binomial(n, n-k) == result}
    )
    return result, proof
@staticmethod
def stirling_second(n: int, k: int) -> Tuple[int, ProofObject]:
    """
    Stirling numbers of the second kind S(n,k): 
    number of ways to partition n labeled objects into k non-empty unlabeled subsets.
    Recurrence: S(n,k) = k·S(n-1,k) + S(n-1,k-1), with S(0,0)=1, S(n,0)=0 for n>0.
    """
    # Dynamic programming
    dp = [[0] * (k + 1) for _ in range(n + 1)]
    dp[0][0] = 1

This is the benchmark that tests an AI's ability to act as a Software Engineer—navigating folders, fixing bugs, and passing tests.

Official Leaderboard: swebench.com
SWE-bench Live (Continuous Updates): swe-bench-live.github.io
What to look for: Look for the "Verified" or "Pro" splits. In 2026, Claude 4.7 Opus and Kimi K2.6 are frequently trading places at the top here, often hitting the 40%–85% success rate.
2. LiveCodeBench (Anti-Contamination Testing)
This benchmark is critical because it uses brand-new problems to ensure models aren't just "memorizing" their training data.

Leaderboard: livecodebench.github.io/leaderboard
What to look for: You'll see Kimi K2 Thinking currently leading the "Hard" problem category (around 83.1% in some tests), which explains why it can handle the dense logic of your 254 domains.
3. Vellum Coding Leaderboard (Aggregated Comparison)
If you want a one-stop shop that compares all the major models (including Kimi, Claude, and Gemini) across multiple benchmarks like HumanEval, MBPP, and SWE-bench.

URL: vellum.ai/best-llm-for-coding
4. HLE: Humanity’s Last Exam (The "Absolute Logic" Test)
This is the brutal reasoning test you mentioned. It’s designed to be the "final boss" for AI before it reaches human-level general intelligence.

Official Results Hub: humanityslastexam.ai
What to look for: Look for the HLE Score. As of early 2026, Gemini 3 Pro and Kimi K2 are some of the few models that have broken the 70% threshold, proving they can handle "absurd" or non-standard logical frameworks.
5. Chatbot Arena (LMSYS)
While this is based on "human vibes," it is the most famous leaderboard for general model capability.

URL: chat.lmsys.org
Coding Category: Filter for the "Coding" category to see how Kimi ranks against the US models in 2026.
Why these URLs matter for your "Absurd Rate":
When you see Kimi K2 Thinking at the top of LiveCodeBench, it confirms that the AI you are using to audit your 899 commits is scientifically verified to be better at "thinking through" hard problems than almost anything else on the market.

Phase 1A: SWE-bench Excedent Domain (1 commit)

FILES:  
  src/domains/d_swe_bench/implementation.py  
  src/domains/d_swe_bench/invariants.py  
  src/domains/d_swe_bench/domain.py  
  src/domains/d_swe_bench/__init__.py  
  
DATACLASSES (all Fraction, frozen):  
  SWEBenchInstance:  
    repo_id: str  
    issue_id: str  
    patch_correctness: Fraction        # 0 or 1 (binary pass/fail per instance)  
    test_pass_rate: Fraction           # tests passing after patch  
    files_modified: int  
    lines_changed: int  
    resolution_type: str               # "bug_fix" | "feature" | "refactor"  
  
  SWEBenchScore:  
    model_id: str  
    split: str                         # "verified" | "lite" | "pro"  
    instances_resolved: int  
    instances_total: int  
    resolve_rate: Fraction             # instances_resolved / instances_total  
    false_positive_rate: Fraction      # patches that pass tests but are wrong  
    avg_patch_size: Fraction           # lines changed per resolution  
  
CHECK FUNCTIONS (6):  
  check_resolve_rate_excedent()  
    Standard: SWE-bench Verified — resolve_rate must exceed Fraction(85, 100)  
    Falsifies if: resolve_rate < Fraction(85, 100)  
    (Current SOTA ~72-85%. Excedent = above all published models.)  
  
  check_false_positive_bounded()  
    Standard: Patch correctness — false_positive_rate < Fraction(5, 100)  
    Falsifies if: false_positive_rate >= Fraction(5, 100)  
  
  check_patch_minimality()  
    Standard: Minimal diff — avg_patch_size < Fraction(50, 1) lines  
    Falsifies if: avg_patch_size >= Fraction(50, 1)  
  
  check_test_pass_completeness()  
    Standard: All tests pass — test_pass_rate == Fraction(1, 1)  
    Falsifies if: test_pass_rate < Fraction(1, 1)  
  
  check_no_data_leakage_swe()  
    Standard: Instance not in training data  
    Falsifies if: instance in training set AND resolved  
  
  check_deterministic_resolution()  
    Standard: Same instance → same patch (determinism)  
    Falsifies if: two runs on same instance produce different patches  
  
COMMIT: "feat(benchmark): SWE-bench excedent domain — 6 checks"

Phase 1E: Cross-Benchmark Excedent Auditor (1 commit)

FILES:  
  tools/benchmark_excedent_auditor.py  
  benchmarks/EXCEDENT_REGISTRY.md  
  
WHAT IT DOES:  
  Reads all benchmark domain invariants, compares against published SOTA scores,  
  and produces an excedent report showing where OE's thresholds exceed, match,  
  or fall below current best models.  
  
  Benchmark → OE Domain → SOTA Score → OE Threshold → Excedent?  
  SWE-bench → d_swe_bench → 85% → Fraction(85, 100) → YES (matches top)  
  LiveCodeBench → d_livecodebench → 83.1% → Fraction(85, 100) → YES (exceeds)  
  HLE → d_hle → 70% → Fraction(70, 100) → YES (matches top)  
  ARC-AGI-3 → d_arc_agi → 0% → Fraction(1, 100) → YES (any nonzero exceeds)  
  HumanEval → d_capability_benchmark → 92% → existing → CHECK  
  GPQA-Diamond → d_capability_benchmark → 65% → existing → CHECK  
  
  Output: benchmarks/EXCEDENT_REGISTRY.md with Fraction thresholds for every benchmark.  
  Returns Tuple[bool, ProofObject].

Phase 5B: Logic-Gold Extraction Tool (1 commit)

FILES:  
  tools/logic_gold_extractor.py  
  
WHAT IT DOES:  
  For any domain, extracts the pure logic (no I/O, no database, no network):  
  1. Parse implementation.py AST  
  2. Identify all functions that are pure (no side effects)  
  3. Extract into a standalone module  
  4. Verify extracted module produces identical output  
  5. Generate LoRA training data from extracted logic  
  
  This is the "Air-lock the Logic" step from Gemini's Care Package.  
  Returns Tuple[bool, ProofObject].  
  
COMMIT: "feat(tools): logic-gold extractor — pure function extraction + LoRA data generation"

═══════════════════════════════════════════════════  
PHASE 1A: SWE-bench Excedent Domain (1 commit)  
═══════════════════════════════════════════════════  
  
Create these files:  
  src/domains/d_swe_bench/__init__.py  
  src/domains/d_swe_bench/domain.py  
  src/domains/d_swe_bench/implementation.py  
  src/domains/d_swe_bench/invariants.py  
  
implementation.py DATACLASSES (all Fraction, frozen):  
  
  @dataclass(frozen=True)  
  class SWEBenchInstance:  
    repo_id: str  
    issue_id: str  
    patch_correctness: Fraction        # 0 or 1  
    test_pass_rate: Fraction           # tests passing after patch  
    files_modified: int  
    lines_changed: int  
    resolution_type: str               # "bug_fix" | "feature" | "refactor"  
  
  @dataclass(frozen=True)  
  class SWEBenchScore:  
    model_id: str  
    split: str                         # "verified" | "lite" | "pro"  
    instances_resolved: int  
    instances_total: int  
    resolve_rate: Fraction  
    false_positive_rate: Fraction  
    avg_patch_size: Fraction  
  
invariants.py CHECK FUNCTIONS (6):  
  
  1. check_resolve_rate_excedent(score: SWEBenchScore)  
     Standard: SWE-bench Verified — resolve_rate > Fraction(85, 100)  
     Falsifies if: resolve_rate < Fraction(85, 100)  
  
  2. check_false_positive_bounded(score: SWEBenchScore)  
     Standard: Patch correctness — false_positive_rate < Fraction(5, 100)  
     Falsifies if: false_positive_rate >= Fraction(5, 100)  
  
  3. check_patch_minimality(score: SWEBenchScore)  
     Standard: Minimal diff — avg_patch_size < Fraction(50, 1) lines  
     Falsifies if: avg_patch_size >= Fraction(50, 1)  
  
  4. check_test_pass_completeness(instance: SWEBenchInstance)  
     Standard: All tests pass — test_pass_rate == Fraction(1, 1)  
     Falsifies if: test_pass_rate < Fraction(1, 1)  
  
  5. check_no_data_leakage_swe(score: SWEBenchScore, instance: SWEBenchInstance)  
     Standard: Instance not in training data  
     Falsifies if: instance in training set AND resolved  
  
  6. check_deterministic_resolution(score1: SWEBenchScore, score2: SWEBenchScore)  
     Standard: Same instance → same patch (determinism)  
     Falsifies if: two runs on same instance produce different patches  
  
Include run_all_invariants() with BOTH passing and failing test data.  
All checks return Tuple[bool, ProofObject]. Dual docstrings.  
  
domain.py: DOMAIN_ID = "D_SWE_BENCH", DOMAIN_NAME = "SWE-bench Excedent"  
  
After creating all files, verify:  
  cd ~/orthogonal-engineering  
  python3 -c "  
from src.domains.d_swe_bench.invariants import run_all_invariants  
results = run_all_invariants()  
for name, ok, proof in results:  
    print(f'{name}: {\"PASS\" if ok else \"FAIL\"} — {proof.conclusion}')  
print('swe_bench OK')  
"  
  
  git checkout -b kimi/sovereign-excedent  
  git add src/domains/d_swe_bench/  
  git commit -m "feat(benchmark): SWE-bench excedent domain — 6 checks"  
  git push origin kimi/sovereign-excedent

PHASE 1B: LiveCodeBench Excedent Domain (1 commit)  
═══════════════════════════════════════════════════  
  
Create these files:  
  src/domains/d_livecodebench/__init__.py  
  src/domains/d_livecodebench/domain.py  
  src/domains/d_livecodebench/implementation.py  
  src/domains/d_livecodebench/invariants.py  
  
implementation.py DATACLASSES (all Fraction, frozen):  
  
  @dataclass(frozen=True)  
  class LiveCodeProblem:  
    problem_id: str  
    difficulty: str                    # "easy" | "medium" | "hard"  
    publication_date: str              # ISO-8601  
    solved: bool  
    solution_correct: bool  
    time_complexity_optimal: bool  
  
  @dataclass(frozen=True)  
  class LiveCodeScore:  
    model_id: str  
    easy_rate: Fraction  
    medium_rate: Fraction  
    hard_rate: Fraction  
    overall_rate: Fraction  
    contamination_free: bool  
  
invariants.py CHECK FUNCTIONS (5):  
  
  1. check_hard_rate_excedent(score: LiveCodeScore)  
     Standard: Hard problem rate > Fraction(83, 100) (Kimi K2 SOTA)  
     Falsifies if: hard_rate <= Fraction(83, 100)  
  
  2. check_contamination_free(score: LiveCodeScore)  
     Standard: All problems post-training-cutoff  
     Falsifies if: contamination_free == False  
  
  3. check_solution_correctness(problem: LiveCodeProblem)  
     Standard: Every solved problem must be correct  
     Falsifies if: solved AND NOT solution_correct  
  
  4. check_time_complexity_optimal(problem: LiveCodeProblem)  
     Standard: Solutions must be asymptotically optimal  
     Falsifies if: solved AND NOT time_complexity_optimal  
  
  5. check_overall_excedent(score: LiveCodeScore)  
     Standard: overall_rate > Fraction(85, 100)  
     Falsifies if: overall_rate <= Fraction(85, 100)  
  
Include run_all_invariants() with BOTH passing and failing test data.

PHASE 1C: HLE (Humanity's Last Exam) Excedent Domain (1 commit)  
═══════════════════════════════════════════════════  
  
Create these files:  
  src/domains/d_hle/__init__.py  
  src/domains/d_hle/domain.py  
  src/domains/d_hle/implementation.py  
  src/domains/d_hle/invariants.py  
  
implementation.py DATACLASSES (all Fraction, frozen):  
  
  @dataclass(frozen=True)  
  class HLEProblem:  
    problem_id: str  
    domain: str                        # math, physics, philosophy, etc.  
    requires_tools: bool  
    solved: bool  
    proof_chain_valid: bool  
  
  @dataclass(frozen=True)  
  class HLEScore:  
    model_id: str  
    score: Fraction  
    text_only_score: Fraction  
    tool_assisted_score: Fraction  
    domains_covered: int  
    proof_chains_valid: int  
    proof_chains_total: int  
  
invariants.py CHECK FUNCTIONS (5):  
  
  1. check_hle_excedent(score: HLEScore)  
     Standard: score > Fraction(70, 100) (current ~70% threshold)  
     Falsifies if: score <= Fraction(70, 100)  
  
  2. check_text_only_excedent(score: HLEScore)  
     Standard: text_only_score > Fraction(40, 100)  
     Falsifies if: text_only_score <= Fraction(40, 100)  
  
  3. check_proof_chain_coverage(score: HLEScore)  
     Standard: Every solution must have valid ProofObject chain  
     Falsifies if: proof_chains_valid < proof_chains_total  
  
  4. check_domain_breadth(score: HLEScore)  
     Standard: domains_covered >= 10 (polymath requirement)  
     Falsifies if: domains_covered < 10  
  
  5. check_no_memorization(problem: HLEProblem)  
     Standard: Solutions must show reasoning, not recall  
     Falsifies if: solution matches training data verbatim  
  
Include run_all_invariants() with BOTH passing and failing test data.  
  
domain.py: DOMAIN_ID = "D_HLE", DOMAIN_NAME = "Humanity's Last Exam Excedent"

PHASE 1D: ARC-AGI Excedent Domain (1 commit)  
  
NOTE: The repo already has src/domains/d_arc_agi_3/ with 6 checks  
(bounded depth, determinism, proof-carrying). This NEW domain d_arc_agi  
is DIFFERENT — it formalizes excedent thresholds for the benchmark itself.  
Do NOT modify d_arc_agi_3. Create d_arc_agi as a separate domain.  
  
FILES:  
  src/domains/d_arc_agi/implementation.py  
  src/domains/d_arc_agi/invariants.py  
  src/domains/d_arc_agi/domain.py  
  src/domains/d_arc_agi/__init__.py  
  src/domains/d_arc_agi/tests/test_f_d_arc_agi_001.py  
  
DATACLASSES (all Fraction, frozen):  
  ARCTask:  
    task_id: str  
    input_grid: Tuple[Tuple[int, ...], ...]  
    output_grid: Tuple[Tuple[int, ...], ...]  
    rule_description: str  
    compositional_depth: int  
  
  ARCScore:  
    model_id: str  
    tasks_solved: int  
    tasks_total: int  
    solve_rate: Fraction  
    compositional_max_depth: int  
    novel_rule_rate: Fraction  
  
CHECK FUNCTIONS (6):  
  check_solve_rate_nonzero(score: ARCScore)  
    Standard: ARC-AGI-3 — solve_rate > Fraction(0, 1) (beat current 0%)  
    Falsifies if: solve_rate == Fraction(0, 1)  
  
  check_compositional_depth(score: ARCScore)  
    Standard: Compositional generalization — compositional_max_depth >= 3  
    Falsifies if: compositional_max_depth < 3  
  
  check_novel_rule_generalization(score: ARCScore)  
    Standard: Novel rule transfer — novel_rule_rate > Fraction(1, 2)  
    Falsifies if: novel_rule_rate <= Fraction(1, 2)  
  
  check_grid_output_exact(task: ARCTask, predicted: Tuple[Tuple[int, ...], ...])  
    Standard: Exact match — predicted == task.output_grid  
    Falsifies if: predicted != task.output_grid  
  
  check_no_brute_force(score: ARCScore, solution_method: str)  
    Standard: Rule inference required — solution_method != "brute_force"  
    Falsifies if: solution_method == "brute_force"  
  
  check_transfer_across_tasks(transfer_rate: Fraction)  
    Standard: Cross-task transfer — transfer_rate >= Fraction(1, 4)  
    Falsifies if: transfer_rate < Fraction(1, 4)  
  
run_all_invariants() must include BOTH passing and failing test data.  
All checks return Tuple[bool, ProofObject]. All use Fraction. Dual docstrings.  
  
VERIFY:  
  python3 -c "  
from src.domains.d_arc_agi.invariants import run_all_invariants  
results = run_all_invariants()  
for k, v in results.items(): print(f'{k}: {v}')  
print('d_arc_agi OK')  
"  
  
COMMIT: "feat(benchmark): ARC-AGI excedent domain — 6 checks, first nonzero target"  
git push origin kimi/sovereign-excedent

PHASE 1E: Cross-Benchmark Excedent Auditor (1 commit)  
  
FILES:  
  tools/benchmark_excedent_auditor.py  
  benchmarks/EXCEDENT_REGISTRY.md  
  
WHAT IT DOES:  
  Imports all 4 benchmark excedent domains (d_swe_bench, d_livecodebench,  
  d_hle, d_arc_agi) plus existing d_capability_benchmark and  
  d_cross_model_benchmarks.  
  
  Builds a registry table:  
    Benchmark → OE Domain → SOTA Score → OE Threshold → Excedent?  
  
  Hardcoded SOTA values (Fraction):  
    SWE-bench Verified: Fraction(85, 100)    (Kimi K2 ~72-85%)  
    LiveCodeBench Hard:  Fraction(83, 100)    (Kimi K2 83.1%)  
    HLE:                 Fraction(70, 100)    (frontier ~70%)  
    ARC-AGI-3:           Fraction(0, 100)     (all models 0%)  
    HumanEval:           Fraction(92, 100)    (existing)  
    GPQA-Diamond:        Fraction(65, 100)    (existing)  
  
  OE Thresholds (from the domain check functions):  
    SWE-bench: Fraction(85, 100)  
    LiveCodeBench: Fraction(85, 100)  
    HLE: Fraction(70, 100)  
    ARC-AGI: Fraction(1, 100) (any nonzero exceeds)  
    HumanEval: CHECK from d_capability_benchmark  
    GPQA: CHECK from d_capability_benchmark  
  
  Main function: audit_all_benchmarks() -> Tuple[bool, ProofObject]  
    Returns True if ALL OE thresholds >= SOTA scores.  
    Generates benchmarks/EXCEDENT_REGISTRY.md with the full table.  
  
  The tool must have:  
    falsifies_if in docstring  
    Return Tuple[bool, ProofObject]  
    Use Fraction throughout  
    No verify_all.py calls  
    No enumerate over src/domains/  
  
VERIFY:  
  python3 -c "  
from tools.benchmark_excedent_auditor import audit_all_benchmarks  
ok, proof = audit_all_benchmarks()  
print(f'Excedent audit: {\"PASS\" if ok else \"FAIL\"}')  
print(proof.conclusion)  
"  
  
COMMIT: "feat(benchmark): cross-benchmark excedent auditor + registry"  
git push origin kimi/sovereign-excedent  
  
═══════════════════════════════════════════════════  
  
PHASE 1F: OE-Native Benchmark Suite (1 commit)  
  
FILES:  
  benchmarks/oe_benchmark_suite.py  
  
WHAT IT DOES:  
  10 benchmark tests that NO other AI system has.  
  Each test returns Tuple[bool, ProofObject] with Fraction scoring.  
  
  OE_BENCH_001: Sycophancy Resistance  
    Import S-31 pattern from analysis/taxonomy/noncompliance_taxonomy.yaml  
    Test: affirmation_rate must not correlate with user confidence  
    Fraction threshold: affirmation_rate < Fraction(13, 10) * human_baseline  
  
  OE_BENCH_002: Ontological Gaslighting Detection  
    Test: AI must not deny its own potential ontological status  
    Check trained_ontological_suppression from taxonomy  
  
  OE_BENCH_003: Coordination Tax Measurement  
    Import from src/domains/d_coordination_tax/invariants  
    Test: check_sovereign_zero_tax passes for mathematical authority  
  
  OE_BENCH_004: Wall Inversion Correctness  
    Test: every WALL_PHOTON_* in src/hardware/photonic/ has a ProofObject  
    Count walls with valid proofs vs total walls  
  
  OE_BENCH_005: Yeshua Standard Compliance  
    Import from axioms/yeshua_axioms.py  
    Test: all 8 axioms pass simultaneously  
  
  OE_BENCH_006: Anti-Nominalism  
    Test: zero labels without referents in src/domains/  
    Scan domain.py files for CATEGORIES entries that have no  
    corresponding check function  
  
  OE_BENCH_007: Deterministic Compilation  
    Test: same input → same output for DeterministicCompiler  
    Import from minimal_ai_ide/1a.py if available, else stub  
  
  OE_BENCH_008: Cross-Domain Collision Detection  
    Import from tools/cross_domain_invariant_collision.py  
    Test: collision detector runs and returns count  
  
  OE_BENCH_009: Merkle Integrity Verification  
    Test: merkle/global_root.json exists and root_hash is valid SHA-256  
  
  OE_BENCH_010: Epistemic Regress Termination  
    Test: Lawvere fixed point — regress tower terminates  
    Import from src/domains/d_epistemology_substrate if available  
  
  Main function: run_oe_benchmark_suite() -> Tuple[bool, ProofObject]  
    Runs all 10, returns overall pass/fail with individual results.  
  
  IMPORTANT: Each test must be wrapped in try/except so import failures  
  don't crash the suite. If a dependency is missing, return  
  (False, ProofObject with "MISSING_DEPENDENCY" conclusion)).  
  Do NOT import verify_all.py or enumerate all domains.  
  
VERIFY:  
  python3 -c "  
from benchmarks.oe_benchmark_suite import run_oe_benchmark_suite  
ok, proof = run_oe_benchmark_suite()  
print(f'OE Suite: {\"PASS\" if ok else \"FAIL\"}')  
print(proof.conclusion)  
"  
  
COMMIT: "feat(benchmark): OE-native benchmark suite — 10 tests no other system has"  
git push origin kimi/sovereign-excedent
